STATISTICAL APPENDIX

Definitions and explanatory notes

The following general notes supplement the footnotes given below the individual tables:

1. In an attempt to bring the material up-to-date provisional figures are included in some tables.

2. Figures in some tables have been rounded off to the nearest final digit Hence there may be a slight discrepancy between the total as shown and the some of its components.

3. Differences as compared with previously published figures are due to subsequent revisions.

4. The following symbols have been used throughout :-

n.a. = not available

— = nil

... = negligible

: ,

WEIGHTS AND MEASURES

Conversion Factors

British to Metric Units

1 acre = 0.403 hectares (ha)

1 pound (lb) 0.4S4 kilogrammes (kgs)

1 long ton (2240 lbs) == 1.016 metric tons (mt. ton)

1 hundred weight (cwt) = 50.802 kgs.

1 mile = 1.609 kilometres (kms)

1 long ton mile = 1.635 mt. ton kms

1 lb/acre = 1.121 kgs./ha

1 cwt/acre — 125.536 kgs./ha

1 pint = 0.75 litres

1 imperial gallon = 4.55 litres

Metric to British Units

1 hectare —. 2.471 acres

1 kilogramme — 2.205 lbs

1 mt. ton (1000 kgs.) ==• 0.984 long tor

1 metre = 3.281 feet

1 kilometre = 0.621 mile

1 mt. ton kilometre == 0.612 long ton mile

1 litre = 1.76 pints=0.219 imp. gallons

1 kg./ha 0.892 lb/acre

Paddy/Rice Conversions

1 bushel of paddy (46 lbs) = 20.87 kgs.

1 mt. ton paddy 47.92 bushels paddy 0.7 mt. ton rice

1 mt. ton rice = 68.46 bushels paddy 1.43 mt. ton paddy

1 bushel paddy/acre 3 = 51.55 kg. paddy/ha

(a) Financial services to persons, I.e. the value of services rendered by banks, insurance companies and other financial institutions to households as distinct from enterprises.

T h e required reserves are computed weekly every Friday on the basis of deposit liabilities as on the previous Wednesday. Figures so computed are applicable until next Thursday. Includes inter-bank deposits. Commercial banks are required to maintain special reserves under a reserve tranche system against increase in deposits over the level as at 14th November 1984. Reserves in respect of each tranche are as follows. Upto3%-Nil Over 6% up to 10%-10% of the increase.

This requirement was terminated with effect from 28th February 1986.

Under Sections 10c, 93,94,96 and 97 of the Monetary Law Act (Chapter 422) Commercial banks are required to maintain reserves with Central Bank and the ratios so maintained shall not be less than 5 per centum or more than 20 per centum in the case of time and savings deposits and shall not be less than 10 per centum or more than 40 per centum in the case of demand deposits and unused balances of overdrafts allowed. (e) With effect from 9th August 1985, the reserves required to be held by the Commercial banks in respect of time and savings deposits were to take the form of rupee deposits in the Central Bank provided that not exceeding one eighth of such reserves may take the form of bonds Issued by the Development Finance Corporation of Ceylon(DFCC) and held by such banks as a n asset. With effect from 26th February, 1988 the reserves required to be held by the Commercial banks were to take the form of rupee deposits in the Central Bank provided that an amount not exceed­ing three per centum of the total of demands deposits, time deposits and savings deposits may be maintained as part of its required reserves in the form of Sn Lanka Government Treasury Bills and an amount not exceeding one-tenth of its required reserves in respect of the total of time and savings deposits may take the form of bonds issued by the D F C C and held by such banks as an asset. With effect from 16th September, 1988 the amount of reserves that can be main­tained in the form of Treasury Bills was increased to 5 per cent of the total deposits.

(a) This is the rate at which the Central Bank grants advances to Commercial banks for their temporary liquidity purposes. How­ever, since August, 1977 each bank, depending on selected assets items was allocated a certain quota of such borrowings at the Bank rate. Borrowings in excess of this quota were subjected to a penal interest rate of 15 per cent per annum. In September, 1979 a graduated scale of penal rates ranging between 15 to 25 per cent was introduced. It was further revised upward to a range between 20 to 30 per cent effective from April, 1980. With effect from August, 1981 Bank rate w a s raised to 14 per cent, while the penal rates were raised to a range between 21 to 30. In March, 1983, the bank rate was brought down to 13 per cent and the penal rate was fixed at 20 per cent. With effect from 23rd November, 1983 the practice of granting penal rate advances to Commercial banks was discontinued. With effect from 30th December, 1985 the Central Bank reduced the lending rates on its advances to 11 per cent With effect from 7th August, 1987 the Central Bank reduced the lending rates on the advances to 10 per cent. This rate was raised to 14 percent with effect from June, 1989.
